(January 2019)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> and 2033, followed by a crewed phase in 2040-2060.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mars_500" title="Mars 500">Mars 500</a> study of 2011 prepared for this manned mission.\n</p><p>Moreover, in order to make crewed flight in deep space toward Mars safer, a <a href="/wiki/Space_weather" title="Space weather">space weather</a> forecast system was to be completed by 2017 with the <a href="/wiki/Kuafu_project" title="Kuafu project">Kuafu</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kuafu_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-kuafu-61">[61]</a></sup> mission satellites placed at the <a href="/wiki/List_of_objects_at_Lagrangian_points#Planned_probes" title="List of objects at Lagrangian points">Lagrangian Point L1</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> However, due to withdrawal first by Canada and then ESA, the project was indefinitely postponed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2006, the Chief Designer of the Shenzhou spacecraft stated in an interview that:\n</p>\n<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: \'Times New Roman\', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">&#8220;\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">&#25630;&#33322;&#22825;&#24037;&#31243;&#19981;&#26159;&#35201;&#36798;&#25104;&#21319;&#31354;&#20043;&#26053;&#65292;<br/>\n<p>&#32780;&#26159;&#35201;&#35753;&#20154;&#21487;&#20197;&#27491;&#24120;&#22312;&#22826;&#31354;&#20013;&#24037;&#20316;&#65292;<br/>\n&#20026;&#23558;&#26469;&#25506;&#32034;&#28779;&#26143;&#12289;&#22303;&#26143;&#31561;&#20316;&#22909;&#20934;&#22791;&#12290;\n</p><p>Space programs are not aimed at sending humans into space <i>per se</i>,<br/>\nbut instead at enabling humans to work normally in space, <br/>\nand prepare for the future exploration of Mars, Saturn, and beyond.\n</p>\n</td>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: \'Times New Roman\', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">&#8221;\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td class="cquotecite" colspan="3" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller; line-height:normal; text-align: right;"><cite>&#8212;&#8201;<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Academy_of_Science" title="Chinese Academy of Science">CAS</a> Academician <a href="/wiki/Qi_Faren" title="Qi Faren">Qi Faren</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></cite>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Space-based_solar_power">Space-based solar power</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chinese_space_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Space-based solar power">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>According to the China Academy of Space Technology (CAST) presentation at the 2015 International Space Development Congress in Toronto, Canada, Chinese interest in <a href="/wiki/Space-based_solar_power" title="Space-based solar power">space-based solar power</a> began in the period 1990&#8211;1995.  By 2011 there was a proposal for a national program, with advocates such as Pioneer Professor Wang Xiji stating in an article for the Ministry of Science and technology that "China had built up a solid industrial foundation, acquired sufficient technology and had enough money to carry out the most ambitious space project in history.  Once completed, the solar station, with a capacity of 100MW, would span at least one square kilometre, dwarfing the International Space Station and becoming the biggest man-made object in space" and "warned that if it did not act quickly, China would let other countries, in particular the US and Japan, take the lead and occupy strategically important locations in space."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Global Security cites a 2011-01 Journal of Rocket propulsion that articulates the need for 620+ launches of their Long March-9 (CZ-9) heavy lift system for the construction of an orbital solar power plant with 10,000 MW capacity massing 50,000 tonnes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E7%A9%BA%E9%96%93%E7%AB%99%E4%BA%8C.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="250" data-file-width="300" decoding="async" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E7%A9%BA%E9%96%93%E7%AB%99%E4%BA%8C.PNG/220px-%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E7%A9%BA%E9%96%93%E7%AB%99%E4%BA%8C.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/10/%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E7%A9%BA%E9%96%93%E7%AB%99%E4%BA%8C.PNG 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E7%A9%BA%E9%96%93%E7%AB%99%E4%BA%8C.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Chinese_large_modular_space_station" title="Chinese large modular space station">Impression of the Chinese Space Station</a> by an artist</div></div></div>\n<p>By 2013 there was a national goal, that "the state has decided that power coming from outside of the earth, such as solar power and development of other space energy resources, is to be China\'s future direction" and the following roadmap was identified: "In 2010, CAST will finish the concept design; in 2020, we will finish the industrial level testing of in-orbit construction and wireless transmissions. In 2025, we will complete the first 100kW SPS demonstration at LEO; and in 2035, the 100MW SPS will have electric generating capacity. Finally in 2050, the first commercial level SPS system will be in operation at GEO."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-67">[67]</a></sup>  The article went on to state that "Since SPS development will be a huge project, it will be considered the equivalent of an Apollo program for energy. In the last century, America\'s leading position in science and technology worldwide was inextricably linked with technological advances associated with implementation of the Apollo program. Likewise, as China\'s current achievements in aerospace technology are built upon with its successive generations of satellite projects in space, China will use its capabilities in space science to assure sustainable development of energy from space."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-67">[67]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2015, the CAST team won the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=International_SunSat_Design_Competition&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="International SunSat Design Competition (page does not exist)">International SunSat Design Competition</a> with their video of a Multi-Rotary Joint concept.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup>  The design was presented in detail in a paper for the Online Journal of Space Communication.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2016, Lt Gen. Zhang Yulin, deputy chief of the [PLA] armament development department of the Central Military Commission, suggested that China would next begin to exploit Earth-Moon space for industrial development. The goal would be the construction of space-based solar power satellites that would beam energy back to Earth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-2">[2]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Goals">Goals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chinese_space_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Goals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The China National Space Administration stated that their long-term goals are:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Improve their standing in the world of space science</li>\n<li>Establish a crewed space station</li>\n<li>Crewed missions to the moon<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Establish a crewed lunar base<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Unmanned mission to Mars</li>\n<li>Exploit Earth-Moon space for industrial development.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_projects">List of projects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chinese_space_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: List of projects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Satellites_and_science">Satellites and science</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chinese_space_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Satellites and science">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space-Based_ASAT_System" title="Space-Based ASAT System">Space-Based ASAT System</a> small and nano-satellites developed by the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Small_Satellite_Research_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Small Satellite Research Institute (page does not exist)">Small Satellite Research Institute</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Academy_of_Space_Technology" title="Chinese Academy of Space Technology">Chinese Academy of Space Technology</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></li>\n<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Double_Star_Mission" title="Double Star Mission">Double Star Mission</a> comprised two satellites launched in 2003 and 2004, jointly with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ESA" title="ESA">ESA</a>, to study the Earth\'s magnetosphere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Earth_observation" title="Earth observation">Earth observation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Remote_sensing" title="Remote sensing">remote sensing</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reconnaissance_satellites" title="Reconnaissance satellites">reconnaissance satellites</a> series: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CBERS" title="CBERS">CBERS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dongfanghong_program" title="Dongfanghong program">Dongfanghong program</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fanhui_Shi_Weixing" title="Fanhui Shi Weixing">Fanhui Shi Weixing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yaogan" title="Yaogan">Yaogan</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ziyuan_3" title="Ziyuan 3">Ziyuan 3</a>.</li>\n<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tianlian_2&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tianlian 2 (page does not exist)">Tianlian 2</a> (&#22825;&#38142;&#20108;&#21495;) Next generation <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Data_relay_satellite" title="Data relay satellite">data relay satellite</a> (DRS) system, based on the DFH-4 satellite bus, with two satellites providing up to 85% coverage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beidou_navigation_system" title="Beidou navigation system">Beidou navigation system</a> or Compass Navigation Satellite System, composed of 60 to 70 satellites, during the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eleventh_Five-Year_Plan_(People%27s_Republic_of_China)" title="Eleventh Five-Year Plan (People\'s Republic of China)">Eleventh Five-Year Plan</a>" period (2006&#8211;2010).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Astrophysics" title="Astrophysics">Astrophysics</a> research, with the launch of the world\'s largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solar_Space_Telescope" title="Solar Space Telescope">Solar Space Telescope</a> in 2008, and <i>Project 973</i> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_Hard_X-Ray_Modulation_Telescope" title="Space Hard X-Ray Modulation Telescope">Space Hard X-Ray Modulation Telescope</a> (&#30828;X&#23556;&#32447;&#35843;&#21046;&#26395;&#36828;&#38236;HXMT) by 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kuafu_project" title="Kuafu project">Kuafu</a> mission satellites for space weather forecasts was planned to be completed by 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kuafu_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-kuafu-61">[61]</a></sup> However, due to withdrawal first by Canada and then ESA, the project was indefinitely postponed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Deep Space Tracking Network with the completion of the <a href="/wiki/Five_hundred_meter_Aperture_Spherical_Telescope" title="Five hundred meter Aperture Spherical Telescope">FAST</a>, the world\'s largest single dish <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radio_antenna" title="Radio antenna">radio antenna</a> of 500 m in Guizhou, and a 3000&#160;km <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VLBI" title="VLBI">VLBI</a> radio antenna.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></li>\n<li>A <i><a href="/wiki/Deep_Impact_(spacecraft)" title="Deep Impact (spacecraft)">Deep Impact</a></i>-style mission to test process of re-directing the direction of an asteroid or comet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Satellite_launch_center">Satellite launch center</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chinese_space_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Satellite launch center">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wenchang_Satellite_Launch_Center" title="Wenchang Satellite Launch Center">Hainan Spaceport</a> Fourth and southernmost space center, will be upgraded to suit the new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Long_March_5_rocket_family" title="Long March 5 rocket family">CZ-5</a> Heavy <a href="/wiki/Expendable_launch_system" title="Expendable launch system">ELV</a> and crewed lunar missions</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Launch_vehicles">Launch vehicles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chinese_space_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Launch vehicles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LM-5D" title="LM-5D">LM-5D</a></li>\n<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Air-Launched_SLV&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Air-Launched SLV (page does not exist)">Air-Launched SLV</a> able to place a 50 kilogram plus payload to 500&#160;km <a href="/wiki/Sun-synchronous_orbit" title="Sun-synchronous orbit">SSO</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kaituozhe-2" title="Kaituozhe-2">Kaituozhe-2</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kaituozhe-1" title="Kaituozhe-1">Kaituozhe-1</a> (&#24320;&#25299;&#32773;&#19968;&#21495;), <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=KT-1A&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="KT-1A (page does not exist)">KT-1A</a> (&#24320;&#25299;&#32773;&#19968;&#21495;&#30002;), <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=KT-2&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="KT-2 (page does not exist)">KT-2</a> (&#24320;&#25299;&#32773;&#20108;&#21495;), <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=KT-2A&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="KT-2A (page does not exist)">KT-2A</a> (&#24320;&#25299;&#32773;&#19968;&#20108;&#30002;) New class of all-solid orbital launch vehicles</li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kaituozhe-1B" title="Kaituozhe-1B">Kaituozhe-1B</a> (&#24320;&#25299;&#32773;&#19968;&#21495;&#20057;) with addition of two solid boosters<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Long_March_1_rocket_family" title="Long March 1 rocket family">CZ-1D</a> based on a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Long_March_1_rocket_family" title="Long March 1 rocket family">CZ-1</a> but with a new N2O4/UDMH second stage</li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Long_March_2_rocket_family" title="Long March 2 rocket family">CZ-2E(A)</a> Intended for launch of Chinese space station modules. Payload capacity up to 14 tons in LEO and 9000 (kN) liftoff thrust developed by 12 rocket engines, with enlarged fairing of 5.20 m in diameter and length of 12.39 m to accommodate large spacecraft<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Long_March_2_rocket_family" title="Long March 2 rocket family">CZ-2F/G</a> Modified <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CZ-2F" title="CZ-2F">CZ-2F</a> without escape tower, specially used for launching unmanned missions such as Shenzhou cargo and space laboratory module with payload capacity up to 11.2 tons in LEO<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Long_March_3_rocket_family" title="Long March 3 rocket family">CZ-3B(A)</a> More powerful Long March rockets using larger-size liquid propellant strap-on motors, with payload capacity up to 13 tons in LEO</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Long_March_3C" title="Long March 3C">CZ-3C</a> Launch vehicle combining <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Long_March_3_rocket_family" title="Long March 3 rocket family">CZ-3B</a> core with two boosters from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Long_March_2_rocket_family" title="Long March 2 rocket family">CZ-2E</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Long_March_5_rocket_family" title="Long March 5 rocket family">Chang Zheng 5</a> Second generation ELV with more efficient and nontoxic propellents (25 tonnes in LEO)</li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chang_Zheng_6" title="Chang Zheng 6">Chang Zheng 6</a> or Small Launch Vehicle, with short launch preparation period, low cost and high reliability, to meet the launch need of small satellites up to 500&#160;kg to 700&#160;km <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sun_synchronous_orbit" title="Sun synchronous orbit">SSO</a>, first flight for 2010; with <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Fan_Ruixiang&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Fan Ruixiang (page does not exist)">Fan Ruixiang</a> (&#33539;&#29790;&#31077;) as Chief designer of the project<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chang_Zheng_7" title="Chang Zheng 7">Chang Zheng 7</a> used for Phase 4 of Lunar Exploration Program (&#23270;&#23077;-4 &#24037;&#31243;), that is permanent base (&#26376;&#38754;&#39547;&#30041;) expected for 2024; Second generation Heavy ELV for lunar and deep space trajectory injection (70 tonnes in LEO), capable of supporting a Soviet <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_Moonshot" title="Soviet Moonshot">L1/L3</a>-like lunar landing mission<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Project_921-3" title="Project 921-3">Project 921-3</a> <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">Space Shuttle</a> &#8211; second generation manned spacecraft <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shenlong_Space_Plane" title="Shenlong Space Plane">Shenlong Spaceplane</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Project_921-3#HTS_Maglev_Launch_Assist_Technology" title="Project 921-3">HTS Maglev Launch Assist Space Shuttle</a> New second generation manned, reusable spacecraft</li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Long_March_9" title="Long March 9">Long March 9</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Long_March_11" title="Long March 11">Long March 11</a></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Space_exploration">Space exploration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chinese_space_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Space exploration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Project_921-1" title="Project 921-1">Project 921-1</a> &#8211; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shenzhou_spacecraft" title="Shenzhou spacecraft">Shenzhou spacecraft</a></li>\n<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Project_921-11&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Project 921-11 (page does not exist)">Project 921-11</a> &#8211; <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=X-11_spacecraft&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="X-11 spacecraft (page does not exist)">X-11 spacecraft</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Project_921-2" title="Project 921-2">Project 921-2</a> &#8211; Chinese Space Laboratory and Chinese Permanent Space Station, short term and then permanent occupation<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Shenzhou_Cargo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Shenzhou Cargo (page does not exist)">Shenzhou Cargo</a> (&#36135;&#36816;&#39134;&#33337;) &#8211; unmanned version of the Shenzhou spacecraft to resupply the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Space_Station" title="Chinese Space Station">Chinese Permanent Space Station</a> and return cargo back to Earth</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tianzhou_(spacecraft)" title="Tianzhou (spacecraft)">Tianzhou</a> &#8211; unmanned cargo vessel to resupply the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Space_Station" title="Chinese Space Station">Chinese Permanent Space Station</a> based on the design of <a href="/wiki/Tiangong-1" title="Tiangong-1">Tiangong-1</a>, not meant for reentry, but usable for garbage disposal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Chinese_Lunar_Exploration_Program" title="Chinese Lunar Exploration Program">Chinese Lunar Exploration Program</a>\n<ul><li>First phase, <a href="/wiki/Chang%27e_1" title="Chang\'e 1">Chang\'e 1</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chang%27e_2" title="Chang\'e 2">Chang\'e 2</a> &#8211; launched in 2007 and 2010</li>\n<li>Second phase, <a href="/wiki/Chang%27e_3" title="Chang\'e 3">Chang\'e 3</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chang%27e_4" title="Chang\'e 4">Chang\'e 4</a> &#8211; launched in 2013 and 2018</li>\n<li>Third phase, <a href="/wiki/Chang%27e_5-T1" title="Chang\'e 5-T1">Chang\'e 5-T1</a> (completed) and <a href="/wiki/Chang%27e_5" title="Chang\'e 5">Chang\'e 5</a> &#8211; to be launched in December 2019 to perform a sample-return.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Fourth phase, <a href="/wiki/Chang%27e_6" title="Chang\'e 6">Chang\'e 6</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Chang%27e_7&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Chang\'e 7 (page does not exist)">Chang\'e 7</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Chang%27e_8&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Chang\'e 8 (page does not exist)">Chang\'e 8</a> - will explore the south pole for natural resources; may 3D-print a structure using regolith.</li>\n<li>Crewed mission: In the 2030s, see <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Lunar_Exploration_Program#Crewed_mission" title="Chinese Lunar Exploration Program">Chinese Lunar Exploration Program#Crewed mission</a></li></ul></li></ul>\n<ul><li>Chinese <a href="/wiki/Exploration_of_Mars" title="Exploration of Mars">exploration of Mars</a> &#8211; The <a href="/wiki/Yinghuo-1" title="Yinghuo-1">Yinghuo-1</a> orbiter was launched in November 2011 in the joint <a href="/wiki/Fobos-Grunt" title="Fobos-Grunt">Fobos-Grunt</a> mission with Russia, but the rocket failed to leave Earth orbit and underwent destructive re-entry on 15 January 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup>  Further planned missions include <a href="/wiki/Rover_(space_exploration)" title="Rover (space exploration)">rover</a>, landers and possible crewed missions in the far future.</li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Deep_space_exploration_roadmap">Deep space exploration roadmap</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chinese_space_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Deep space exploration roadmap">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In 2018, Chinese researchers proposed a deep space exploration roadmap to explore Mars, an asteroid, Jupiter, and further targets, within the 2020-2030 timeframe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Planning2030_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Planning2030-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2018UNOOSA_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-2018UNOOSA-96">[96]</a></sup> Proposed robotic missions include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><b>Asteroid Exploration Mission</b>, proposed for launch around 2022-2024.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2018UNOOSA_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-2018UNOOSA-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spacedaily20180426_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-spacedaily20180426-97">[97]</a></sup> Mission goals include asteroid <a href="/wiki/Planetary_flyby" title="Planetary flyby">flyby observations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Remote_sensing" title="Remote sensing">global remote sensing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lander_(spacecraft)" title="Lander (spacecraft)">unmanned landing</a>, and possible <a href="/wiki/Sample-return_mission" title="Sample-return mission">sample return</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Planning2030_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-Planning2030-95">[95]</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>Mars Sample Return Mission (HX-2)</b>, proposed for launch around 2028-2030.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2018UNOOSA_96-2"><a href="#cite_note-2018UNOOSA-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gbtimes20170714_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-gbtimes20170714-98">[98]</a></sup> Mission goals include <a href="/wiki/In_situ#Space-related" title="In situ">in-situ</a> topography and soil composition analysis, deep interior investigations to probe the planet\'s origins and geologic evolution, and sample return.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Planning2030_95-2"><a href="#cite_note-Planning2030-95">[95]</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>Jupiter System Exploration Mission</b>, proposed for launch around 2029-2030,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2018UNOOSA_96-3"><a href="#cite_note-2018UNOOSA-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spacedaily20180426_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-spacedaily20180426-97">[97]</a></sup> and arriving at <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">Jupiter</a> around 2036.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gbtimes20170714_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-gbtimes20170714-98">[98]</a></sup> Mission goals include orbital <a href="/wiki/Exploration_of_Jupiter" title="Exploration of Jupiter">exploration of Jupiter</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Galilean_moons" title="Galilean moons">four largest moons</a>, study of the <a href="/wiki/Magnetohydrodynamics" title="Magnetohydrodynamics">magnetohydrodynamics</a> in the Jupiter system, and investigation of the internal composition of Jupiter\'s atmosphere and moons,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Planning2030_95-3"><a href="#cite_note-Planning2030-95">[95]</a></sup> especially <a href="/wiki/Ganymede_(moon)" title="Ganymede (moon)">Ganymede</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gbtimes20170714_98-2"><a href="#cite_note-gbtimes20170714-98">[98]</a></sup></li>\n<li>A <a href="/wiki/Exploration_of_Uranus" title="Exploration of Uranus"><b>mission to Uranus</b></a>, though tentative, has been proposed for implementation after 2030, with a probe arriving in the 2040s. It is presumed to be part of a future planetary flyby phase of exploration, and would study the <a href="/wiki/Solar_wind" title="Solar wind">solar wind</a> and <a href="/wiki/Interplanetary_magnetic_field" title="Interplanetary magnetic field">interplanetary magnetic field</a> as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Planning2030_95-4"><a href="#cite_note-Planning2030-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gbtimes20170714_98-3"><a href="#cite_note-gbtimes20170714-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spacenews20170710_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-spacenews20170710-99">[99]</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>These missions, with the exception of the Uranus mission, have either been officially approved or are in the study phase as of June 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spacenews20170710_99-1"><a href="#cite_note-spacenews20170710-99">[99]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chinese_space_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Center for Space Science and Applied Research (CSSAR), was founded in 1987 by merging the former Institute of Space Physics (i.e. the Institute of Applied Geophysics founded in 1958) and the Center for Space Science and Technology (founded in 1978). The research fields of CSSAR mainly cover 1. Space Engineering Technology; 2. Space Weather Exploration, Research, and Forecasting; 3. Microwave Remote Sensing and Information Technology.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chinese_space_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div
